</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Issue<br/><span style="font-weight:normal"><i><a href="#Wives,_concubines,_and_children">Among others</a></i></span></th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="plainlist">

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Carolingians" title="Template:Carolingians"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Carolingians" title="Template talk:Carolingians"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Carolingians&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Charlemagne</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">SHAR</span>-lə-mayn, -⁠<span style="font-size:90%">MAYN</span></i></a>, <small>French: </small><span class="IPA" lang="fr-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʃaʁləmaɲ]</a></span>) or <b>Charles the Great</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Carolus Magnus</i>; 2 April 747<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[a]</a></sup> – 28 January 814), a member of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_dynasty" title="Carolingian dynasty">Carolingian dynasty</a>, was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_the_Franks" title="King of the Franks">King of the Franks</a> from 768, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_the_Lombards" title="King of the Lombards">King of the Lombards</a> from 774, and the first <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor of the Romans</a> from 800. Charlemagne succeeded in uniting the majority of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">central Europe</a> and was the first recognized emperor to rule from western Europe after the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">fall of the Western Roman Empire</a> around three centuries earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBecher2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidKbbMcYpuQswCpgPA96_96]_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBecher2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidKbbMcYpuQswCpgPA96_96]-4">[3]</a></sup> The expanded Frankish state that Charlemagne founded was the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a>. He was <a href="/wiki/Canonization" title="Canonization">canonized</a> by <a href="/wiki/Antipope_Paschal_III" title="Antipope Paschal III">Antipope Paschal III</a>—an act later treated as invalid—and he is now regarded by some as <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">beatified</a> (which is a step on the path to <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">sainthood</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.
</p><p>Charlemagne was the eldest son of <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Short" title="Pepin the Short">Pepin the Short</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bertrada_of_Laon" title="Bertrada of Laon">Bertrada of Laon</a>. He was born before their <a href="/wiki/Marriage_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Marriage in the Catholic Church">canonical marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarbero200412–_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarbero200412–-5">[4]</a></sup> He became king of the Franks in 768 following his father's death, and was initially co-ruler with his brother <a href="/wiki/Carloman_I" title="Carloman I">Carloman I</a> until the latter's death in 771.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> As sole ruler, he continued his father's policy towards protection of the papacy and became its sole defender, removing the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombards</a> from power in northern <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and leading an incursion into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_Spain" title="Muslim Spain">Muslim Spain</a>. He also campaigned against the <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a> to his east, <a href="/wiki/Capitulatio_de_partibus_Saxoniae" title="Capitulatio de partibus Saxoniae">Christianizing them (upon penalty of death)</a> which led to events such as the <a href="/wiki/Massacre_of_Verden" title="Massacre of Verden">Massacre of Verden</a>. He reached the height of his power in 800 when he was <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Coronation of the Holy Roman Emperor">crowned Emperor of the Romans</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_III" title="Pope Leo III">Pope Leo III</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a> at <a href="/wiki/Old_St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="Old St. Peter's Basilica">Old St. Peter's Basilica</a> in Rome.
</p><p>Charlemagne has been called the "Father of Europe" (<i>Pater Europae</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> as he united most of Western Europe for the first time since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_era" title="Classical era">classical era</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, as well as uniting parts of Europe that had never been under Frankish or Roman rule. His reign spurred the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Renaissance" title="Carolingian Renaissance">Carolingian Renaissance</a>, a period of energetic cultural and intellectual activity within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Church" title="Western Church">Western Church</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> viewed Charlemagne less favourably, due to his support of the <a href="/wiki/Filioque" title="Filioque">filioque</a> and the Pope's preference of him as emperor over the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>'s first female monarch, <a href="/wiki/Irene_of_Athens" title="Irene of Athens">Irene of Athens</a>. These and other disputes led to the eventual split of <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Constantinople</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Schism_of_1054" title="Great Schism of 1054">Great Schism of 1054</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGregory2005251–52_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGregory2005251–52-8">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[b]</a></sup>
</p><p>Charlemagne died in 814 after contracting an infectious lung disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> He was laid to rest in the <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral" title="Aachen Cathedral">Aachen Cathedral</a>, in his imperial capital city of <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>. He married at least four times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Will_Durant_Chronique_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Will_Durant_Chronique-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlemagne_Britannica_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Charlemagne_Britannica-2">[2]</a></sup> and had three legitimate sons who lived to adulthood. Only the youngest of them, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a>, survived to succeed him. Charlemagne and his predecessors are the direct ancestors of many of Europe's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_houses" title="Royal houses">royal houses</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_dynasty" title="Capetian dynasty">Capetian dynasty</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[c]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Ottonian_dynasty" title="Ottonian dynasty">Ottonian dynasty</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[d]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Luxembourg" title="House of Luxembourg">House of Luxembourg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[e]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Ivrea" title="House of Ivrea">House of Ivrea</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[f]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[g]</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Wives,_concubines,_and_children"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Wives, concubines, and children</span></a>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Children"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Children</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_nicknames">Names and nicknames</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names and nicknames">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3564" data-file-width="2443" decoding="async" height="321" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg/220px-Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg/330px-Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg/440px-Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Domschatz_Bueste1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bust_of_Charlemagne" title="Bust of Charlemagne">Bust of Charlemagne</a>, an idealised portrayal and reliquary said to contain Charlemagne's <a href="/wiki/Calvaria_(skull)" title="Calvaria (skull)">skull cap</a>, is located at <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral_Treasury" title="Aachen Cathedral Treasury">Aachen Cathedral Treasury</a>, and can be regarded as the most famous depiction of the ruler.</div></div></div><p>The name Charlemagne (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small>English: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">SHAR</span>-lə-mayn, -⁠<span style="font-size:90%">MAYN</span></i></a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[16]</a></sup> by which the emperor is normally known in English, comes from the French <i>Charles-le-magne</i>, meaning "Charles the Great".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[h]</a></sup> In modern German, <i>Karl der Große</i> has the same meaning. His given name was simply Charles (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>Carolus</i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> <i>Karlus</i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance" title="Gallo-Romance">Romance</a> <i>Karlo</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson20192_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson20192-25">[17]</a></sup> He was named after his grandfather, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Martel" title="Charles Martel">Charles Martel</a>, a choice which intentionally marked him as Martel's true heir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBecher200342–43_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBecher200342–43-26">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>The nickname <i>magnus</i> (great) may have been associated with him already in his lifetime, but this is not certain. The contemporary Latin <i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Frankish_Annals" title="Royal Frankish Annals">Royal Frankish Annals</a></i> routinely call him <i>Carolus magnus rex</i>, "Charles the great king".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarbero2004413_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarbero2004413-27">[19]</a></sup> As a nickname, it is only certainly attested in the works of the <a href="/wiki/Poeta_Saxo" title="Poeta Saxo">Poeta Saxo</a> around 900 and it only became standard in all the lands of his former empire around 1000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFried20164_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFried20164-28">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>Charles' achievements gave a new meaning to <a href="/wiki/Charles" title="Charles">his name</a>. In many <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Europe" title="Languages of Europe">languages of Europe</a>, the very word for "king" derives from his name; e.g., <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">król</i>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">король (korol')</span>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">král</i>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>: <i lang="sk">kráľ</i>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">király</i>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>: <i lang="lt">karalius</i>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">karalis</i>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">король</span>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>: <span lang="mk">крал</span>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">крал</span>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">Serbo-Croatian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sh-Cyrl">краљ/kralj</span>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">kral</i>. This development parallels that of the name of the <a href="/wiki/Caesar_(title)" title="Caesar (title)">Caesars</a> in the original Roman Empire, which became <i>kaiser</i> and <i>tsar</i> (or <i>czar</i>), among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson2013_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson2013-29">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_background">Political background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Political background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francia_714.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="1252" decoding="async" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Francia_714.png/280px-Francia_714.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Francia_714.png/420px-Francia_714.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Francia_714.png/560px-Francia_714.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francia_714.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Francia, early 8th century</div></div></div></div>
<p>By the 6th century, the western <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> tribe of the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> had been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_Christianity" title="Germanic Christianity">Christianised</a>, due in considerable measure to the Catholic conversion of <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">Clovis I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldmanMason2006270,_274–75_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldmanMason2006270,_274–75-30">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">Francia</a>, ruled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merovingians" title="Merovingians">Merovingians</a>, was the most powerful of the kingdoms that succeeded the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1999161–72_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1999161–72-31">[23]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tertry" title="Battle of Tertry">Battle of Tertry</a>, the Merovingians declined into powerlessness, for which they have been dubbed the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rois_fain%C3%A9ants" title="Rois fainéants">rois fainéants</a></i> ("do-nothing kings").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFouracre20055–8_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFouracre20055–8-32">[24]</a></sup> Almost all government powers were exercised by their chief officer, the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_the_palace" title="Mayor of the palace">mayor of the palace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[i]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 687, <a href="/wiki/Pepin_of_Herstal" title="Pepin of Herstal">Pepin of Herstal</a>, mayor of the palace of <a href="/wiki/Austrasia" title="Austrasia">Austrasia</a>, ended the strife between various kings and their mayors with his victory at Tertry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrassetto2003292_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrassetto2003292-34">[25]</a></sup> He became the sole governor of the entire Frankish kingdom. Pepin was the grandson of two important figures of the Austrasian Kingdom: Saint <a href="/wiki/Arnulf_of_Metz" title="Arnulf of Metz">Arnulf of Metz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepin_of_Landen" title="Pepin of Landen">Pepin of Landen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrassetto2003292–93_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrassetto2003292–93-35">[26]</a></sup> Pepin of Herstal was eventually succeeded by his son Charles, later known as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Martel" title="Charles Martel">Charles Martel</a> (Charles the Hammer).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaldmanMason2006271_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaldmanMason2006271-36">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>After 737, Charles governed the Franks in lieu of a king and declined to call himself <i>king</i>. Charles was succeeded in 741 by his sons <a href="/wiki/Carloman_(mayor_of_the_palace)" title="Carloman (mayor of the palace)">Carloman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Short" title="Pepin the Short">Pepin the Short</a>, the father of Charlemagne. In 743, the brothers placed <a href="/wiki/Childeric_III" title="Childeric III">Childeric III</a> on the throne to curb separatism in the periphery. He was the last Merovingian king. Carloman resigned office in 746, preferring to enter the church as a monk. Pepin brought the question of the kingship before <a href="/wiki/Pope_Zachary" title="Pope Zachary">Pope Zachary</a>, asking whether it was logical for a king to have no royal power. The pope handed down his decision in 749, decreeing that it was better for Pepin to be called king, as he had the powers of high office as Mayor, so as not to confuse the hierarchy. He, therefore, ordered him to become the <i>true king</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-France/Pippin_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-France/Pippin-37">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 750, Pepin was elected by an assembly of the Franks, anointed by the archbishop, and then raised to the office of king. The Pope branded Childeric III as "the false king" and ordered him into a monastery. The Merovingian dynasty was thereby replaced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolingian" title="Carolingian">Carolingian</a> dynasty, named after Charles Martel. In 753, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Stephen_II" title="Pope Stephen II">Pope Stephen II</a> fled from Italy to Francia, appealing to Pepin for assistance for the rights of St. Peter. He was supported in this appeal by Carloman, Charles' brother. In return, the pope could provide only legitimacy. He did this by again anointing and confirming Pepin, this time adding his young sons Carolus (Charlemagne) and Carloman to the royal patrimony. They thereby became heirs to the realm that already covered most of western Europe. In 754, Pepin accepted the Pope's invitation to visit Italy on behalf of St. Peter's rights, dealing successfully with the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-France/Pippin_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-France/Pippin-37">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the Carolingians, the Frankish kingdom spread to encompass an area including most of Western Europe; the later east–west division of the kingdom formed the basis for modern <a href="/wiki/History_of_France" title="History of France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Germany" title="History of Germany">Germany</a>. Orman<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOman1914409–10_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOman1914409–10-39">[30]</a></sup> portrays the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a> (843) between the warring grandsons of Charlemagne as the foundation event of an independent <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> under its first king <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bald" title="Charles the Bald">Charles the Bald</a>; an independent Germany under its first king <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_German" title="Louis the German">Louis the German</a>; and an independent intermediate state stretching from the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> along the borderlands to south of Rome under <a href="/wiki/Lothair_I" title="Lothair I">Lothair I</a>, who retained the title of emperor and the capitals <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> and Rome without the jurisdiction. The middle kingdom had broken up by 890 and partly absorbed into the Western kingdom (later France) and the Eastern kingdom (Germany) and the rest developing into smaller "buffer" states that exist between France and Germany to this day, namely <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_to_power">Rise to power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rise to power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="693" data-file-width="723" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg/220px-Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg/330px-Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg/440px-Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chauss%C3%A9e-Brunehault.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman road connecting Tongeren to the Herstal region. Jupille and Herstal, near Liege, are located in the lower right corner</div></div></div>
<p>The most likely date of Charlemagne's birth is reconstructed from several sources. The date of 742—calculated from <a href="/wiki/Einhard" title="Einhard">Einhard</a>'s date of death of January 814 at age 72—predates the marriage of his parents in 744. The year given in the <i><a href="/wiki/Annales_Petaviani" title="Annales Petaviani">Annales Petaviani</a></i>, 747, would be more likely, except that it contradicts Einhard and a few other sources in making Charlemagne sixty-seven years old at his death. The month and day of 2 April are based on a calendar from <a href="/wiki/Lorsch_Abbey" title="Lorsch Abbey">Lorsch Abbey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baldwin_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baldwin-40">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 747, <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> fell on 2 April, a coincidence that likely would have been remarked upon by chroniclers but was not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[32]</a></sup> If Easter was being used as the beginning of the calendar year, then 2 April 747 could have been, by modern reckoning, April 748 (not on Easter). The date favoured by the preponderance of evidence<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarbero200412–_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarbero200412–-5">[4]</a></sup> is 2 April 742, based on Charlemagne's age at the time of his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baldwin_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Baldwin-40">[31]</a></sup> This date supports the concept that Charlemagne was technically an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegitimacy" title="Illegitimacy">illegitimate</a> child, although that is not mentioned by Einhard in either since he was born out of wedlock; Pepin and Bertrada were bound by a private contract or <a href="/wiki/Friedelehe" title="Friedelehe">Friedelehe</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarbero200412–_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarbero200412–-5">[4]</a></sup> at the time of his birth, but did not marry until 744.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Charlemagne's exact birthplace is unknown, although historians have suggested Aachen in modern-day Germany, and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a> (<a href="/wiki/Herstal" title="Herstal">Herstal</a>) in present-day <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> as possible locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[34]</a></sup> Aachen and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Liège">Liège</a> are close to the region whence the Merovingian and Carolingian families originated. Other cities have been suggested, including <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCren" title="Düren">Düren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gauting" title="Gauting">Gauting</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCrlenbach" title="Mürlenbach">Mürlenbach</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Quierzy" title="Quierzy">Quierzy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%BCm" title="Prüm">Prüm</a>. No definitive evidence resolves the question.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox" style="width: 220px; float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><tbody><tr><th href="/wiki/Khan_Academy" title="Khan Academy">Khan Academy</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Charlemagne was the eldest child of <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Short" title="Pepin the Short">Pepin the Short</a> (714 – 24 September 768, reigned from 751) and his wife <a href="/wiki/Bertrada_of_Laon" title="Bertrada of Laon">Bertrada of Laon</a> (720 – 12 July 783), daughter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribert_of_Laon" title="Caribert of Laon">Caribert of Laon</a>. Many historians consider Charlemagne (Charles) to have been illegitimate, although some state that this is arguable,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[36]</a></sup> because Pepin did not marry Bertrada until 744, which was after Charles' birth; this status did not exclude him from the succession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1998[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid05IVoPSfb48CpgPA32_32–]_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1998[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid05IVoPSfb48CpgPA32_32–]-46">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>Records name only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carloman_I,_King_of_the_Franks" title="Carloman I, King of the Franks">Carloman</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gisela_(daughter_of_Pepin_the_Short)" title="Gisela (daughter of Pepin the Short)">Gisela</a>, and three short-lived children named Pepin, Chrothais and Adelais as his younger siblings.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It would be folly, I think, to write a word concerning Charles' birth and infancy, or even his boyhood, for nothing has ever been written on the subject, and there is no one alive now who can give information on it.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/Einhard" title="Einhard">Einhard</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._4._Plan_of_This_Work_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._4._Plan_of_This_Work-49">[40]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ambiguous_high_office">Ambiguous high office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ambiguous high office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_the_palace" title="Mayor of the palace">Mayor of the palace</a></div>
<p>The most powerful officers of the Frankish people, the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_the_palace" title="Mayor of the palace">Mayor of the Palace</a> (<i>Maior Domus</i>) and one or more kings (<i>rex</i>, <i>reges</i>), were appointed by the election of the people. Elections were not periodic, but were held as required to elect officers <i>ad quos summa imperii pertinebat</i>, "to whom the highest matters of state pertained". Evidently, interim decisions could be made by the Pope, which ultimately needed to be ratified using an assembly of the people that met annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._1._The_Merovingian_Family_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._1._The_Merovingian_Family-50">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before he was elected king in 751, Pepin was initially a mayor, a high office he held "as though hereditary" (<i>velut hereditario fungebatur</i>). Einhard explains that "the honour" was usually "given by the people" to the distinguished, but Pepin the Great and his brother Carloman the Wise received it as though hereditary, as had their father, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Martel" title="Charles Martel">Charles Martel</a>. There was, however, a certain ambiguity about quasi-inheritance. The office was treated as joint property: one Mayorship held by two brothers jointly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[42]</a></sup> Each, however, had his own geographic jurisdiction. When Carloman decided to resign, becoming ultimately a Benedictine at <a href="/wiki/Monte_Cassino" title="Monte Cassino">Monte Cassino</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard,_putative741–829Years_745,_746_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard,_putative741–829Years_745,_746-52">[43]</a></sup> the question of the disposition of his quasi-share was settled by the pope. He converted the mayorship into a kingship and awarded the joint property to Pepin, who gained the right to pass it on by inheritance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War-53">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>This decision was not accepted by all family members. Carloman had consented to the temporary tenancy of his own share, which he intended to pass on to his son, Drogo, when the inheritance should be settled at someone's death. By the Pope's decision, in which Pepin had a hand, Drogo was to be disqualified as an heir in favour of his cousin Charles. He took up arms in opposition to the decision and was joined by <a href="/wiki/Grifo_(noble)" title="Grifo (noble)">Grifo</a>, a half-brother of Pepin and Carloman, who had been given a share by Charles Martel, but was stripped of it and held under loose arrest by his half-brothers after an attempt to seize their shares by military action. Grifo perished in combat in the Battle of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Maurienne" title="Saint-Jean-de-Maurienne">Saint-Jean-de-Maurienne</a> while Drogo was hunted down and taken into custody.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins199832–33_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins199832–33-54">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <i>Life</i>, Pepin died in Paris on 24 September 768, whereupon the kingship passed jointly to his sons, "with divine assent" (<i>divino nutu</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._3._Charlemagne's_Accession_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._3._Charlemagne's_Accession-55">[46]</a></sup>  The Franks "in general assembly" (<i>generali conventu</i>) gave them both the rank of a king (<i>reges</i>) but "partitioned the whole body of the kingdom equally" (<i>totum regni corpus ex aequo partirentur</i>). The <i>annals</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard,_putative741–829Year_768_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard,_putative741–829Year_768-56">[47]</a></sup> tell a slightly different version, with the king dying at <a href="/wiki/Saint-Denis,_Seine-Saint-Denis" title="Saint-Denis, Seine-Saint-Denis">St-Denis</a>, near Paris. The two "lords" (<i>domni</i>) were "elevated to kingship" (<i>elevati sunt in regnum</i>), Charles on 9 October in <a href="/wiki/Noyon" title="Noyon">Noyon</a>, Carloman on an unspecified date in <a href="/wiki/Soissons" title="Soissons">Soissons</a>. If born in 742, Charles was 26 years old, but he had been campaigning at his father's right hand for several years, which may help to account for his military skill. <a href="/wiki/Carloman_I" title="Carloman I">Carloman</a> was 17.
</p><p>The language, in either case, suggests that there were not two inheritances, which would have created distinct kings ruling over distinct kingdoms, but a single joint inheritance and a joint kingship tenanted by two equal kings, Charles and his brother Carloman. As before, distinct jurisdictions were awarded. Charles received Pepin's original share as Mayor: the outer parts of the kingdom bordering on the sea, namely <a href="/wiki/Neustria" title="Neustria">Neustria</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a>, and the northern parts of <a href="/wiki/Austrasia" title="Austrasia">Austrasia</a>; while Carloman was awarded his uncle's former share, the inner parts: southern Austrasia, <a href="/wiki/Septimania" title="Septimania">Septimania</a>, eastern Aquitaine, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burgundy_(region)" title="Burgundy (region)">Burgundy</a>, Provence, and <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>, lands bordering <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>. The question of whether these jurisdictions were joint shares reverting to the other brother if one brother died or were inherited property passed on to the descendants of the brother who died was never definitely settled. It came up repeatedly over the succeeding decades until the grandsons of Charlemagne created distinct sovereign kingdoms.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aquitainian_rebellion">Aquitainian rebellion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Aquitainian rebellion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_of_a_new_Aquitaine">Formation of a new Aquitaine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Formation of a new Aquitaine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a></div>
<p>In southern <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a> had been Romanised and people spoke a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">Romance language</a>. Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> had been populated by peoples who spoke various languages, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_language" title="Celtic language">Celtic</a>, but these had now been mostly replaced by Romance languages. Between Aquitaine and Hispania were the <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Euskaldunak</a>, Latinised to <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins198732_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins198732-57">[48]</a></sup> whose country, Vasconia, extended, according to the distributions of place names attributable to the Basques, mainly in the western <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> but also as far south as the upper river <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> in Spain and as far north as the river <a href="/wiki/Garonne" title="Garonne">Garonne</a> in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987105_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987105-58">[49]</a></sup> The French name <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a> derives from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasconia" title="Vasconia">Vasconia</a>. The Romans were never able to subjugate the whole of Vasconia. The soldiers they recruited for the Roman legions from those parts they did submit and where they founded the region's first cities were valued for their fighting abilities. The border with Aquitaine was at <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>.
</p><p>In about 660, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Vasconia" title="Duchy of Vasconia">Duchy of Vasconia</a> united with the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Aquitaine" title="Duke of Aquitaine">Duchy of Aquitaine</a> to form a single realm under <a href="/wiki/Felix_of_Aquitaine" title="Felix of Aquitaine">Felix of Aquitaine</a>, ruling from Toulouse. This was a joint kingship with a Basque Duke, <a href="/wiki/Lupus_I_of_Aquitaine" title="Lupus I of Aquitaine">Lupus I</a>. <i>Lupus</i> is the Latin translation of Basque Otsoa, "wolf".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglassBilbao200536–37_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglassBilbao200536–37-59">[50]</a></sup> At Felix's death in 670 the joint property of the kingship reverted entirely to Lupus. As the Basques had no law of joint inheritance but relied on <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">primogeniture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lupus_I_of_Aquitaine" title="Lupus I of Aquitaine">Lupus</a> in effect founded a hereditary dynasty of Basque rulers of an expanded Aquitaine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987100_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987100-60">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_of_Aquitaine_by_the_Carolingians">Acquisition of Aquitaine by the Carolingians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Acquisition of Aquitaine by the Carolingians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Umayyad conquest of Hispania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al-Andalus732.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="327" data-file-width="349" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Al-Andalus732.jpg/220px-Al-Andalus732.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Al-Andalus732.jpg/330px-Al-Andalus732.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Al-Andalus732.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al-Andalus732.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorish" title="Moorish">Moorish</a> <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> in 732</div></div></div>
<p>The Latin chronicles of the end of <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> omit many details, such as identification of characters, filling in the gaps and reconciliation of numerous contradictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[52]</a></sup> Muslim sources, however, present a more coherent view, such as in the <i>Ta'rikh iftitah al-Andalus</i> ("History of the Conquest of al-Andalus") by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Q%C5%AB%E1%B9%ADiyya" title="Ibn al-Qūṭiyya">Ibn al-Qūṭiyya</a> ("the son of the Gothic woman", referring to the granddaughter of <a href="/wiki/Wittiza" title="Wittiza">Wittiza</a>, the last Visigothic king of a united Hispania, who married a Moor). Ibn al-Qūṭiyya, who had another, much longer name, must have been relying to some degree on family oral tradition.
</p><p>According to Ibn al-Qūṭiyya<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJamesIbn_al-Qūṭiyya200949_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJamesIbn_al-Qūṭiyya200949-62">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wittiza" title="Wittiza">Wittiza</a>, the last Visigothic king of a united Hispania, died before his three sons, Almund, Romulo, and Ardabast reached maturity. Their mother was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_regent" title="Queen regent">queen regent</a> at <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Roderic" title="Roderic">Roderic</a>, army chief of staff, staged a rebellion, capturing <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="Córdoba, Spain">Córdoba</a>. He chose to impose a joint rule over distinct jurisdictions on the true heirs. Evidence of a division of some sort can be found in the distribution of coins imprinted with the name of each king and in the king lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins2004131–32_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins2004131–32-63">[54]</a></sup> Wittiza was succeeded by Roderic, who reigned for seven and a half years, followed by Achila (Aquila), who reigned three and a half years. If the reigns of both terminated with the incursion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saracens" title="Saracens">Saracens</a>, then Roderic appears to have reigned a few years before the majority of Achila. The latter's kingdom was securely placed to the northeast, while Roderic seems to have taken the rest, notably modern <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.
</p><p>The Saracens crossed the mountains to claim Ardo's <a href="/wiki/Septimania" title="Septimania">Septimania</a>, only to encounter the Basque dynasty of Aquitaine, always the allies of the Goths. <a href="/wiki/Odo_the_Great" title="Odo the Great">Odo the Great</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a> was at first victorious at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toulouse_(721)" title="Battle of Toulouse (721)">Battle of Toulouse</a> in 721.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglassBilbao200540_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglassBilbao200540-64">[55]</a></sup> Saracen troops gradually massed in Septimania and, in 732, an army under Emir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdul_Rahman_Al_Ghafiqi" title="Abdul Rahman Al Ghafiqi">Abdul Rahman Al Ghafiqi</a> advanced into Vasconia, and Odo was defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_River_Garonne" title="Battle of the River Garonne">Battle of the River Garonne</a>. They took <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a> and were advancing towards <a href="/wiki/Tours" title="Tours">Tours</a> when Odo, powerless to stop them, appealed to his arch-enemy, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Martel" title="Charles Martel">Charles Martel</a>, mayor of the Franks. In one of the first of the lightning marches for which the Carolingian kings became famous, Charles and his army appeared in the path of the Saracens between Tours and <a href="/wiki/Poitiers" title="Poitiers">Poitiers</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tours" title="Battle of Tours">Battle of Tours</a> decisively defeated and killed al-Ghafiqi. The Moors returned twice more, each time suffering defeat at Charles' hands—at the River Berre near Narbonne in 737<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard200724_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard200724-65">[56]</a></sup> and in the <a href="/wiki/Dauphin%C3%A9" title="Dauphiné">Dauphiné</a> in 740.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis2009_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis2009-66">[57]</a></sup> Odo's price for salvation from the Saracens was incorporation into the Frankish kingdom, a decision that was repugnant to him and also to his heirs.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_and_recovery_of_Aquitaine">Loss and recovery of Aquitaine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Loss and recovery of Aquitaine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After the death of his father, <a href="/wiki/Hunald_I" title="Hunald I">Hunald I</a> allied himself with free <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a>. However, Odo had ambiguously left the kingdom jointly to his two sons, Hunald and Hatto. The latter, loyal to Francia, now went to war with his brother over full possession. Victorious, Hunald blinded and imprisoned his brother, only to be so stricken by conscience that he resigned and entered the church as a monk to do penance. The story is told in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annales_Mettenses_priores" title="Annales Mettenses priores">Annales Mettenses priores</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freeman1904_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Freeman1904-67">[58]</a></sup> His son <a href="/wiki/Waiofar" title="Waiofar">Waifer</a> took an early inheritance, becoming duke of Aquitaine and ratifying the alliance with Lombardy. Waifer, deciding to honour it, repeated his father's decision, which he justified by arguing that any agreements with Charles Martel became invalid on Martel's death. Since <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a> was now Pepin's inheritance because of the earlier assistance given by Charles Martel, according to some, the latter and his son, the young Charles, hunted down Waifer, who could only conduct a guerrilla war, and executed him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERussell193088_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERussell193088-68">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among the contingents of the Frankish army were <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarians</a> under <a href="/wiki/Tassilo_III,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Tassilo III, Duke of Bavaria">Tassilo III, Duke of Bavaria</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agilofing" title="Agilofing">Agilofing</a>, the hereditary Bavarian ducal family. <a href="/wiki/Grifo_(noble)" title="Grifo (noble)">Grifo</a> had installed himself as Duke of Bavaria, but Pepin replaced him with a member of the ducal family yet a child, Tassilo, whose protector he had become after the death of his father. The loyalty of the Agilolfings was perpetually in question, but Pepin exacted numerous oaths of loyalty from Tassilo. However, the latter had married <a href="/wiki/Liutperga" title="Liutperga">Liutperga</a>, a daughter of <a href="/wiki/Desiderius" title="Desiderius">Desiderius</a>, king of <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a>. At a critical point in the campaign, Tassilo left the field with all his Bavarians. Out of reach of Pepin, he repudiated all loyalty to Francia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKitterick2008118–25_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKitterick2008118–25-69">[60]</a></sup> Pepin had no chance to respond as he grew ill and died within a few weeks after Waifer's execution.
</p><p>The first event of the brothers' reign was the uprising of the Aquitainians and <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascons</a> in 769, in that territory split between the two kings. One year earlier, Pepin had finally defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waifer_of_Aquitaine" title="Waifer of Aquitaine">Waifer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Aquitaine" title="Duke of Aquitaine">Duke of Aquitaine</a>, after waging a destructive, ten-year war against Aquitaine. Now, <a href="/wiki/Hunald_II" title="Hunald II">Hunald II</a> led the Aquitainians as far north as <a href="/wiki/Angoul%C3%AAme" title="Angoulême">Angoulême</a>. Charles met Carloman, but Carloman refused to participate and returned to Burgundy. Charles went to war, leading an army to <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>, where he built a fortified camp on the mound at <a href="/wiki/Fronsac,_Gironde" title="Fronsac, Gironde">Fronsac</a>. Hunald was forced to flee to the court of Duke <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lupo_II_of_Gascony" title="Lupo II of Gascony">Lupus II of Gascony</a>. Lupus, fearing Charles, turned Hunald over in exchange for peace, and Hunald was put in a monastery. Gascon lords also surrendered, and Aquitaine and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Vasconia" title="Duchy of Vasconia">Gascony</a> were finally fully subdued by the Franks.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_to_Desiderata">Marriage to Desiderata</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Marriage to Desiderata">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The brothers maintained lukewarm relations with the assistance of their mother Bertrada, but in 770 Charles signed a treaty with Duke <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tassilo_III_of_Bavaria" title="Tassilo III of Bavaria">Tassilo III of Bavaria</a> and married a Lombard Princess (commonly known today as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desiderata,_wife_of_Charlemagne" title="Desiderata, wife of Charlemagne">Desiderata</a>), the daughter of King Desiderius, to surround Carloman with his own allies. Though <a href="/wiki/Pope_Stephen_III" title="Pope Stephen III">Pope Stephen III</a> first opposed the marriage with the Lombard princess, he found little to fear from a Frankish-Lombard alliance.
</p><p>Less than a year after his marriage, Charlemagne repudiated Desiderata and married a 13-year-old Swabian named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hildegard,_wife_of_Charlemagne" title="Hildegard, wife of Charlemagne">Hildegard</a>. The repudiated Desiderata returned to her father's court at <a href="/wiki/Pavia" title="Pavia">Pavia</a>. Her father's wrath was now aroused, and he would have gladly allied with Carloman to defeat Charles. Before any open hostilities could be declared, however, Carloman died on 5 December 771, apparently of natural causes. Carloman's widow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerberge,_wife_of_Carloman" title="Gerberge, wife of Carloman">Gerberga</a> fled to Desiderius' court with her sons for protection.
</p>
<h2><span id="Wives.2C_concubines.2C_and_children"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Wives,_concubines,_and_children">Wives, concubines, and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Wives, concubines, and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_dynasty" title="Carolingian dynasty">Carolingian dynasty</a></div>
<p>Charlemagne had eighteen children with seven of his ten known wives or concubines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Will_Durant_Chronique_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Will_Durant_Chronique-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlemagne_Britannica_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Charlemagne_Britannica-2">[2]</a></sup> Nonetheless, he had only four legitimate grandsons, the four sons of his fourth son, Louis. In addition, he had a grandson (<a href="/wiki/Bernard_of_Italy" title="Bernard of Italy">Bernard of Italy</a>, the only son of his third son, <a href="/wiki/Pepin_of_Italy" title="Pepin of Italy">Pepin of Italy</a>), who was illegitimate but included in the line of inheritance. Among his descendants are several royal dynasties, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capetian" title="Capetian">Capetian</a> dynasties. By consequence, most if not all established European noble families ever since can genealogically trace some of their background to Charlemagne.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Children">Children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="488" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg/170px-Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg/255px-Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg/340px-Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karl_der_Grosse_-_Pippin_von_Italien.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charlemagne (left) and <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Hunchback" title="Pepin the Hunchback">Pepin the Hunchback</a> (10th-century copy of 9th-century original)</div></div></div>
<p>During the first peace of any substantial length (780–782), Charles began to appoint his sons to positions of authority. In 781, during a visit to Rome, he made his two youngest sons kings, crowned by the Pope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[k]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[l]</a></sup> The elder of these two, <a href="/wiki/Pepin_of_Italy" title="Pepin of Italy">Carloman</a>, was made the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Italy" title="King of Italy">king of Italy</a>, taking the Iron Crown that his father had first worn in 774, and in the same ceremony was renamed "Pepin"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War-53">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campaigns_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campaigns-79">[67]</a></sup> (not to be confused with Charlemagne's eldest, possibly illegitimate son, <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Hunchback" title="Pepin the Hunchback">Pepin the Hunchback</a>). The younger of the two, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis</a>, became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Aquitaine" title="King of Aquitaine">King of Aquitaine</a>. Charlemagne ordered Pepin and Louis to be raised in the customs of their kingdoms, and he gave their regents some control of their subkingdoms, but kept the real power, though he intended his sons to inherit their realms. He did not tolerate insubordination in his sons: in 792, he banished Pepin the Hunchback to <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%BCm_Abbey" title="Prüm Abbey">Prüm Abbey</a> because the young man had joined a rebellion against him.
</p><p>Charles was determined to have his children educated, including his daughters, as his parents had instilled the importance of learning in him at an early age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[68]</a></sup> His children were also taught skills in accord with their aristocratic status, which included training in riding and weaponry for his sons, and embroidery, spinning and weaving for his daughters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>The sons fought many wars on behalf of their father. <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Younger" title="Charles the Younger">Charles</a> was mostly preoccupied with the Bretons, whose border he shared and who insurrected on at least two occasions and were easily put down. He also fought the Saxons on multiple occasions. In 805 and 806, he was sent into the Böhmerwald (modern <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>) to deal with the Slavs living there (Bohemian tribes, ancestors of the modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czech_people" title="Czech people">Czechs</a>). He subjected them to Frankish authority and devastated the valley of the Elbe, forcing tribute from them. Pippin had to hold the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avar</a> and Beneventan borders and fought the <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> to his north. He was uniquely poised to fight the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> when that conflict arose after Charlemagne's imperial coronation and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venetia_(region)" title="Venetia (region)">Venetian</a> rebellion. Finally, Louis was in charge of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_March" title="Spanish March">Spanish March</a> and fought the Duke of Benevento in southern Italy on at least one occasion. He took <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in a great siege in 797.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="447" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/220px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/330px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/440px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charlemagne instructing his son <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a></div></div></div>
<p>Charlemagne kept his daughters at home with him and refused to allow them to contract <a href="/wiki/Marriage#Religion" title="Marriage">sacramental marriages</a> (though he originally condoned an engagement between his eldest daughter Rotrude and <a href="/wiki/Constantine_VI" title="Constantine VI">Constantine VI</a> of Byzantium, this engagement was annulled when Rotrude was 11).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[70]</a></sup> Charlemagne's opposition to his daughters' marriages may possibly have intended to prevent the creation of <a href="/wiki/Cadet_branch" title="Cadet branch">cadet branches</a> of the family to challenge the main line, as had been the case with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tassilo_III_of_Bavaria" title="Tassilo III of Bavaria">Tassilo of Bavaria</a>. However, he tolerated their extramarital relationships, even rewarding their common-law husbands and treasuring the illegitimate grandchildren they produced for him. He also refused to believe stories of their wild behaviour. After his death the surviving daughters were banished from the court by their brother, the pious Louis, to take up residence in the convents they had been bequeathed by their father. At least one of them, Bertha, had a recognised relationship, if not a marriage, with <a href="/wiki/Angilbert" title="Angilbert">Angilbert</a>, a member of Charlemagne's court circle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBecher2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidKbbMcYpuQswCpgPA122_122]_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBecher2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidKbbMcYpuQswCpgPA122_122]-83">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKitterick200891_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKitterick200891-84">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_campaigns">Italian campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Italian campaigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_the_Lombard_kingdom">Conquest of the Lombard kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Conquest of the Lombard kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="556" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg/220px-Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg/330px-Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg/440px-Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_and_Pope_Adrian_I.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Frankish king Charlemagne was a devout Catholic and maintained a close relationship with the papacy throughout his life. In 772, when <a href="/wiki/Pope_Adrian_I" title="Pope Adrian I">Pope Adrian I</a> was threatened by invaders, the king rushed to Rome to provide assistance. Shown here, the pope asks Charlemagne for help at a meeting near Rome.</div></div></div>
<p>At his succession in 772, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Adrian_I" title="Pope Adrian I">Pope Adrian I</a> demanded the return of certain cities in the former <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">exarchate of Ravenna</a> in accordance with a promise at the succession of Desiderius. Instead, Desiderius took over certain papal cities and invaded the <a href="/wiki/Pentapolis" title="Pentapolis">Pentapolis</a>, heading for Rome. Adrian sent ambassadors to Charlemagne in autumn requesting he enforce the policies of his father, Pepin. Desiderius sent his own ambassadors denying the pope's charges. The ambassadors met at <a href="/wiki/Thionville" title="Thionville">Thionville</a>, and Charlemagne upheld the pope's side. Charlemagne demanded what the pope had requested, but Desiderius swore never to comply. Charlemagne and his uncle <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernhard,_son_of_Charles_Martel" title="Bernhard, son of Charles Martel">Bernard</a> crossed the Alps in 773 and chased the Lombards back to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Pavia_(773%E2%80%9374)" title="Siege of Pavia (773–74)">Pavia, which they then besieged</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kohn2006_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kohn2006-85">[73]</a></sup> Charlemagne temporarily left the siege to deal with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adelchis" title="Adelchis">Adelchis</a>, son of Desiderius, who was raising an army at <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a>. The young prince was chased to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adriatic" title="Adriatic">Adriatic</a> littoral and fled to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> to plead for assistance from <a href="/wiki/Constantine_V" title="Constantine V">Constantine V</a>, who was waging war with <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgaria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War-53">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>The siege lasted until the spring of 774 when Charlemagne visited the pope in Rome. There he confirmed <a href="/wiki/Donation_of_Pepin" title="Donation of Pepin">his father's grants of land</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campaigns_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campaigns-79">[67]</a></sup> with some later chronicles falsely claiming that he also expanded them, granting <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emilia_(region_of_Italy)" title="Emilia (region of Italy)">Emilia</a>, Venice and <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>. The pope granted him the title <i><a href="/wiki/Patrician_(post-Roman_Europe)" title="Patrician (post-Roman Europe)">patrician</a></i>. He then returned to Pavia, where the Lombards were on the verge of surrendering. In return for their lives, the Lombards surrendered and opened the gates in early summer. Desiderius was sent to the <a href="/wiki/Abbey" title="Abbey">abbey</a> of <a href="/wiki/Corbie" title="Corbie">Corbie</a>, and his son Adelchis died in Constantinople, a patrician. Charles, unusually, had himself crowned with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_Crown_of_Lombardy" title="Iron Crown of Lombardy">Iron Crown</a> and made the magnates of Lombardy pay homage to him at Pavia. Only Duke <a href="/wiki/Arechis_II_of_Benevento" title="Arechis II of Benevento">Arechis II of Benevento</a> refused to submit and proclaimed independence. Charlemagne was then master of Italy as king of the Lombards. He left Italy with a garrison in Pavia and a few Frankish counts in place the same year.
</p><p>Instability continued in Italy. In 776, Dukes <a href="/wiki/Hrodgaud_of_Friuli" title="Hrodgaud of Friuli">Hrodgaud of Friuli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hildeprand_of_Spoleto" title="Hildeprand of Spoleto">Hildeprand of Spoleto</a> rebelled. Charlemagne rushed back from <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a> and defeated the Duke of Friuli in battle; the Duke was slain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War_53-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880ch._6._Lombard_War-53">[44]</a></sup> The Duke of Spoleto signed a treaty. Their co-conspirator, Arechis, was not subdued, and Adelchis, their candidate in <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantium</a>, never left that city. Northern Italy was now faithfully his.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Italy">Southern Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Southern Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 787, Charlemagne directed his attention towards the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Benevento" title="Duchy of Benevento">Duchy of Benevento</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHodgkin188969_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHodgkin188969-87">[75]</a></sup> where <a href="/wiki/Arechis_II_of_Benevento" title="Arechis II of Benevento">Arechis II</a> was reigning independently with the self-given title of <a href="/wiki/Princeps" title="Princeps">Princeps</a>. Charlemagne's siege of <a href="/wiki/Salerno" title="Salerno">Salerno</a> forced Arechis into submission. However, after Arechis II's death in 787, his son <a href="/wiki/Grimoald_III_of_Benevento" title="Grimoald III of Benevento">Grimoald III</a> proclaimed the Duchy of Benevento newly independent. Grimoald was attacked many times by Charles' or his sons' armies, without achieving a definitive victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHodgkin188985–86_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHodgkin188985–86-88">[76]</a></sup> Charlemagne lost interest and never again returned to <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">Southern Italy</a> where Grimoald was able to keep the Duchy free from Frankish <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Carolingian_expansion_to_the_south">Carolingian expansion to the south</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Carolingian expansion to the south">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vasconia_and_the_Pyrenees">Vasconia and the Pyrenees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Vasconia and the Pyrenees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The destructive war led by Pepin in Aquitaine, although brought to a satisfactory conclusion for the Franks, proved the Frankish power structure south of the <a href="/wiki/Loire" title="Loire">Loire</a> was feeble and unreliable. After the defeat and death of <a href="/wiki/Waiofar" title="Waiofar">Waiofar</a> in 768, while Aquitaine submitted again to the Carolingian dynasty, a new rebellion broke out in 769 led by Hunald II, a possible son of Waifer. He took refuge with the ally Duke <a href="/wiki/Lupus_II_of_Gascony" title="Lupus II of Gascony">Lupus II of Gascony</a>, but probably out of fear of Charlemagne's reprisal, Lupus handed him over to the new King of the Franks to whom he pledged loyalty, which seemed to confirm the peace in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Vasconia" title="Duchy of Vasconia">the Basque area</a> south of the <a href="/wiki/Garonne" title="Garonne">Garonne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-89">[77]</a></sup> In the campaign of 769, Charlemagne seems to have followed a policy of "overwhelming force" and avoided a major pitched battle<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wary of new Basque uprisings, Charlemagne seems to have tried to contain Duke Lupus's power by appointing <a href="/wiki/Seguin_I_of_Gascony" title="Seguin I of Gascony">Seguin</a> as the Count of Bordeaux (778) and other counts of Frankish background in bordering areas (<a href="/wiki/History_of_Toulouse#768–877:_Carolingian_Franks_and_the_Kingdom_of_Aquitaine" title="History of Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_F%C3%A9zensac" title="County of Fézensac">County of Fézensac</a>). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Basque_people#Early_Middle_Ages" title="History of the Basque people">Basque</a> Duke, in turn, seems to have contributed decisively or schemed the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Roncevaux_Pass" title="Battle of Roncevaux Pass">Battle of Roncevaux Pass</a> (referred to as "Basque treachery"). The defeat of Charlemagne's army in Roncevaux (778) confirmed his determination to rule directly by establishing the Kingdom of Aquitaine (ruled by <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a>) based on a power base of Frankish officials, distributing lands among colonisers and allocating lands to the Church, which he took as an ally. A Christianisation programme was put in place across the high <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> (778).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-89">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>The new political arrangement for Vasconia did not sit well with local lords. As of 788 <a href="/wiki/Adalric_of_Gascony" title="Adalric of Gascony">Adalric</a> was fighting and capturing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torson_of_Toulouse" title="Torson of Toulouse">Chorson</a>, Carolingian Count of Toulouse. He was eventually released, but Charlemagne, enraged at the compromise, decided to depose him and appointed his trustee <a href="/wiki/William_of_Gellone" title="William of Gellone">William of Gellone</a>. William, in turn, fought the Basques and defeated them after banishing Adalric (790).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-89">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p>From 781 (<a href="/wiki/County_of_Pallars" title="County of Pallars">Pallars</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Ribagorza" title="County of Ribagorza">Ribagorça</a>) to 806 (<a href="/wiki/Pamplona#Early_Middle_Ages" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a> under Frankish influence), taking the County of Toulouse for a power base, Charlemagne asserted Frankish authority over the Pyrenees by subduing the south-western marches of Toulouse (790) and establishing vassal counties on the southern Pyrenees that were to make up the <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">Marca Hispanica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis196540_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis196540-91">[79]</a></sup> As of 794, a Frankish vassal, the Basque lord Belasko (<i>al-Galashki</i>, 'the Gaul') ruled <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lava" title="Álava">Álava</a>, but Pamplona remained under Cordovan and local control up to 806. Belasko and the counties in the Marca Hispánica provided the necessary base to attack the <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Andalusians</a> (an expedition led by <a href="/wiki/William_of_Gellone" title="William of Gellone">William Count of Toulouse</a> and Louis the Pious to capture Barcelona in 801). Events in the Duchy of Vasconia (rebellion in Pamplona, <a href="/wiki/Aznar_Gal%C3%ADndez_I" title="Aznar Galíndez I">count overthrown in Aragon</a>, Duke Seguin of Bordeaux deposed, uprising of the Basque lords, etc.) were to prove it ephemeral upon Charlemagne's death.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roncesvalles_campaign">Roncesvalles campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Roncesvalles campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbasid-Carolingian_Alliance" title="Abbasid-Carolingian Alliance">Abbasid-Carolingian Alliance</a></div>
