<p>According to the Muslim historian <a href="/wiki/Ibn_al-Athir" title="Ibn al-Athir">Ibn al-Athir</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">Diet</a> of <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a> had received the representatives of the Muslim rulers of <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Girona" title="Girona">Girona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huesca" title="Huesca">Huesca</a>. Their masters had been cornered in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd_ar-Rahman_I" title="Abd ar-Rahman I">Abd ar-Rahman I</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">Umayyad</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emir_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Emir of Córdoba">emir of Cordova</a>. These "Saracen" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorish" title="Moorish">Moorish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muwallad" title="Muwallad">Muwallad</a>) rulers offered their homage to the king of the Franks in return for military support. Seeing an opportunity to extend <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a> and his own power, and believing the Saxons to be a fully conquered nation, Charlemagne agreed to go to Spain.
</p><p>In 778, he led the Neustrian army across the Western <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, while the Austrasians, Lombards, and Burgundians passed over the Eastern Pyrenees. The armies met at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saragossa" title="Saragossa">Saragossa</a> and Charlemagne received the homage of the Muslim rulers, Sulayman al-Arabi and Kasmin ibn Yusuf, but the city did not fall for him. Indeed, Charlemagne faced the toughest battle of his career. The Muslims forced him to retreat, so he decided to go home, as he could not trust the <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a>, whom he had subdued by conquering <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>. He turned to leave Iberia, but as his army was crossing back through the Pass of <a href="/wiki/Roncesvalles" title="Roncesvalles">Roncesvalles</a>, one of the most famous events of his reign occurred: the Basques attacked and destroyed his rearguard and baggage train. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Roncevaux_Pass" title="Battle of Roncevaux Pass">Battle of Roncevaux Pass</a>, though less a battle than a skirmish, left many famous dead, including the <a href="/wiki/Seneschal" title="Seneschal">seneschal</a> Eggihard, the count of the palace Anselm, and the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/warden" title="wikt:warden">warden</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breton_March" title="Breton March">Breton March</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roland" title="Roland">Roland</a>, inspiring the subsequent creation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Song_of_Roland" title="The Song of Roland">The Song of Roland</a></i> (<i>La Chanson de Roland</i>), regarded as the first major work in the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contact_with_the_Saracens">Contact with the Saracens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Contact with the Saracens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harun-Charlemagne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="765" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Harun-Charlemagne.jpg/280px-Harun-Charlemagne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Harun-Charlemagne.jpg/420px-Harun-Charlemagne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Harun-Charlemagne.jpg/560px-Harun-Charlemagne.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harun-Charlemagne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harun_al-Rashid" title="Harun al-Rashid">Harun al-Rashid</a> receiving a delegation of Charlemagne in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, by Julius Köckert (1864)</div></div></div>
<p>The conquest of Italy brought Charlemagne in contact with the <a href="/wiki/Saracen" title="Saracen">Saracens</a> who, at the time, controlled the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>. Charlemagne's eldest son, <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Hunchback" title="Pepin the Hunchback">Pepin the Hunchback</a>, was much occupied with Saracens in Italy. Charlemagne conquered <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> at an unknown date and in 799 the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>. The islands were often attacked by Saracen pirates, but the counts of <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> and Tuscany (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boniface_I_of_Tuscany" title="Boniface I of Tuscany">Boniface</a>) controlled them with large fleets until the end of Charlemagne's reign. Charlemagne even had contact with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caliph" title="Caliph">caliphal</a> court in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. In 797 (or possibly 801), the caliph of Baghdad, <a href="/wiki/Harun_al-Rashid" title="Harun al-Rashid">Harun al-Rashid</a>, presented Charlemagne with an <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a> named <a href="/wiki/Abul-Abbas" title="Abul-Abbas">Abul-Abbas</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Clock" title="Clock">clock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heck2007_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heck2007-92">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wars_with_the_Moors">Wars with the Moors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Wars with the Moors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2018</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a>, the struggle against the Moors continued unabated throughout the latter half of his reign. Louis was in charge of the Spanish border. In 785, his men captured Girona permanently and extended Frankish control into the <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalan</a> littoral for the duration of Charlemagne's reign (the area remained nominally Frankish until the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Corbeil_(1258)" title="Treaty of Corbeil (1258)">Treaty of Corbeil</a> in 1258). The Muslim chiefs in the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Islamic Spain</a> were constantly rebelling against Cordovan authority, and they often turned to the Franks for help. The Frankish border was slowly extended until 795, when Girona, <a href="/wiki/Cardona,_Spain" title="Cardona, Spain">Cardona</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ausona" title="Ausona">Ausona</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Urgell" title="County of Urgell">Urgell</a> were united into the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_March" title="Spanish March">Spanish March</a>, within the old duchy of <a href="/wiki/Septimania" title="Septimania">Septimania</a>.
</p><p>In 797, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, the greatest city of the region, fell to the Franks when Zeid, its governor, rebelled against Cordova and, failing, handed it to them. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umayyad" title="Umayyad">Umayyad</a> authority recaptured it in 799. However, Louis of Aquitaine marched the entire army of his kingdom over the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> and besieged it for two years, wintering there from 800 to 801, when it capitulated. The Franks continued to press forward against the <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">emir</a>. They probably took <a href="/wiki/Tarragona" title="Tarragona">Tarragona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tortosa_(808%E2%80%93809)" title="Siege of Tortosa (808–809)">forced the submission of Tortosa</a> in 809. The last conquest brought them to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> and gave them raiding access to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">Valencia</a>, prompting the Emir <a href="/wiki/Al-Hakam_I" title="Al-Hakam I">al-Hakam I</a> to recognise their conquests in 813.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_campaigns">Eastern campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Eastern campaigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saxon_Wars">Saxon Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Saxon Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Wars" title="Saxon Wars">Saxon Wars</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1205" data-file-width="1591" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg/280px-Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg/420px-Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg/560px-Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frankish_Empire_481_to_814-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charlemagne's additions to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Kingdom" title="Frankish Kingdom">Frankish Kingdom</a></div></div></div>
<p>Charlemagne was engaged in almost constant warfare throughout his reign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[81]</a></sup> often at the head of his elite <i><a href="/wiki/Scara" title="Scara">scara</a></i> bodyguard squadrons. In the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Wars" title="Saxon Wars">Saxon Wars</a>, spanning thirty years and eighteen battles, he conquered <a href="/wiki/Old_Saxony" title="Old Saxony">Saxonia</a> and proceeded to convert it to Christianity.
</p><p>The Germanic <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a> were divided into four subgroups in four regions. Nearest to <a href="/wiki/Austrasia" title="Austrasia">Austrasia</a> was <a href="/wiki/Westphalia" title="Westphalia">Westphalia</a> and farthest away was <a href="/wiki/Eastphalia" title="Eastphalia">Eastphalia</a>. Between them was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engria" title="Engria">Engria</a> and north of these three, at the base of the <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a> peninsula, was <a href="/wiki/Nordalbingia" title="Nordalbingia">Nordalbingia</a>.
</p><p>In his first campaign, in 773, Charlemagne forced the Engrians to submit and cut down an <a href="/wiki/Irminsul" title="Irminsul">Irminsul</a> pillar near <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[82]</a></sup> The campaign was cut short by his first expedition to Italy. He returned in 775, marching through Westphalia and conquering the Saxon fort at <a href="/wiki/Sigiburg" title="Sigiburg">Sigiburg</a>. He then crossed Engria, where he defeated the Saxons again. Finally, in Eastphalia, he defeated a Saxon force, and its leader <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hessi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hessi (page does not exist)">Hessi</a> converted to Christianity. Charlemagne returned through Westphalia, leaving encampments at Sigiburg and <a href="/wiki/Eresburg" title="Eresburg">Eresburg</a>, which had been important Saxon bastions. He then controlled Saxony with the exception of Nordalbingia, but Saxon resistance had not ended.
</p><p>Following his subjugation of the Dukes of Friuli and Spoleto, Charlemagne returned rapidly to Saxony in 776, where a rebellion had destroyed his fortress at Eresburg. The Saxons were once again defeated, but their main leader, <a href="/wiki/Widukind" title="Widukind">Widukind</a>, escaped to Denmark, his wife's home. Charlemagne built a new camp at <a href="/wiki/Karlstadt_am_Main" title="Karlstadt am Main">Karlstadt</a>. In 777, he called a national diet at Paderborn to integrate Saxony fully into the Frankish kingdom. Many Saxons were baptised as Christians.
</p><p>In the summer of 779, he again invaded Saxony and reconquered Eastphalia, Engria and Westphalia. At a diet near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lippe" title="Lippe">Lippe</a>, he divided the land into missionary districts and himself assisted in several mass baptisms (780). He then returned to Italy and, for the first time, the Saxons did not immediately revolt. Saxony was peaceful from 780 to 782.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne,_empereur_d%27Occident,_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind,_785,_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1863" data-file-width="2198" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Charlemagne%2C_empereur_d%27Occident%2C_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind%2C_785%2C_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg/220px-Charlemagne%2C_empereur_d%27Occident%2C_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind%2C_785%2C_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Charlemagne%2C_empereur_d%27Occident%2C_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind%2C_785%2C_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg/330px-Charlemagne%2C_empereur_d%27Occident%2C_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind%2C_785%2C_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Charlemagne%2C_empereur_d%27Occident%2C_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind%2C_785%2C_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg/440px-Charlemagne%2C_empereur_d%27Occident%2C_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind%2C_785%2C_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne,_empereur_d%27Occident,_re%C3%A7oit_la_soumission_de_Wittekind,_785,_por_Ary_Scheffer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charlemagne receiving the submission of <a href="/wiki/Widukind" title="Widukind">Widukind</a> at <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a> in 785, painted c. 1840 by <a href="/wiki/Ary_Scheffer" title="Ary Scheffer">Ary Scheffer</a></div></div></div>
<p>He returned to Saxony in 782 and instituted a code of law and appointed counts, both Saxon and Frank. The laws were draconian on religious issues; for example, the <i><a href="/wiki/Capitulatio_de_partibus_Saxoniae" title="Capitulatio de partibus Saxoniae">Capitulatio de partibus Saxoniae</a></i> prescribed death to Saxon pagans who refused to convert to Christianity. This led to renewed conflict. That year, in autumn, Widukind returned and led a new revolt. In response, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verden,_Germany" title="Verden, Germany">Verden</a> in Lower Saxony, Charlemagne is recorded as having ordered the execution of 4,500 Saxon prisoners by beheading, known as the <a href="/wiki/Massacre_of_Verden" title="Massacre of Verden">Massacre of Verden</a> ("Verdener Blutgericht"). The killings triggered three years of renewed bloody warfare. During this war, the <a href="/wiki/East_Frisia" title="East Frisia">East Frisians</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Lauwers" title="Lauwers">Lauwers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a> joined the Saxons in revolt and were finally subdued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[83]</a></sup> The war ended with Widukind accepting baptism.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrassetto2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidyW-GfElbafQCpgPA368_"Widukind"_p._368]_96-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrassetto2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidyW-GfElbafQCpgPA368_"Widukind"_p._368]-96'>[84]</a></sup> The Frisians afterwards asked for missionaries to be sent to them and a bishop of their own nation, <a href="/wiki/Ludger" title="Ludger">Ludger</a>, was sent. Charlemagne also promulgated a law code, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lex_Frisonum" title="Lex Frisonum">Lex Frisonum</a></i>, as he did for most subject peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thereafter, the Saxons maintained the peace for seven years, but in 792 Westphalia again rebelled. The Eastphalians and Nordalbingians joined them in 793, but the insurrection was unpopular and was put down by 794. An Engrian rebellion followed in 796, but the presence of Charlemagne, Christian Saxons and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">Slavs</a> quickly crushed it. The last insurrection occurred in 804, more than thirty years after Charlemagne's first campaign against them, but also failed. According to Einhard:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The war that had lasted so many years was at length ended by their acceding to the terms offered by the King; which were renunciation of their national religious customs and the worship of devils, acceptance of the sacraments of the Christian faith and religion, and union with the Franks to form one people.
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Submission_of_Bavaria">Submission of Bavaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Submission of Bavaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3255" data-file-width="2530" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg/170px-Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg/255px-Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg/340px-Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_Agostino_Cornacchini_Vatican_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Equestrian_statue_of_Charlemagne_(Cornacchini)" title="Equestrian statue of Charlemagne (Cornacchini)">Equestrian statue of Charlemagne</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Agostino_Cornacchini" title="Agostino Cornacchini">Agostino Cornacchini</a> (1725), <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>By 774, Charlemagne had invaded the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Lombards" title="Kingdom of the Lombards">Kingdom of Lombardy</a>, and he later annexed the Lombardian territories and assumed its crown, placing the <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a> under Frankish protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated30_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated30-98">[86]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Spoleto" title="Duchy of Spoleto">Duchy of Spoleto</a> south of Rome was acquired in 774, while in the central western parts of Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a> was absorbed and the Bavarian policy continued of establishing tributary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marches" title="Marches">marches</a>, (borders protected in return for tribute or taxes) among the <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> Serbs and Czechs. The remaining power confronting the Franks in the east were the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>. However, Charlemagne acquired other Slavic areas, including <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated30_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated30-98">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 789, Charlemagne turned to <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>. He claimed that <a href="/wiki/Tassilo_III,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Tassilo III, Duke of Bavaria">Tassilo III, Duke of Bavaria</a> was an unfit ruler, due to his oath-breaking. The charges were exaggerated, but Tassilo was deposed anyway and put in the monastery of <a href="/wiki/Jumi%C3%A8ges" title="Jumièges">Jumièges</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[87]</a></sup> In 794, Tassilo was made to renounce any claim to Bavaria for himself and his family (the <a href="/wiki/Agilolfings" title="Agilolfings">Agilolfings</a>) at the <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">synod</a> of <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>; he formally handed over to the king all of the rights he had held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1998[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid05IVoPSfb48CpgPA87_87–]_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1998[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid05IVoPSfb48CpgPA87_87–]-100">[88]</a></sup> Bavaria was subdivided into Frankish counties, as had been done with Saxony.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Avar_campaigns">Avar campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Avar campaigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 788, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avars</a>, an Asian nomadic group that had settled down in what is today <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (Einhard called them <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>), invaded Friuli and Bavaria. Charlemagne was preoccupied with other matters until 790 when he marched down the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and ravaged Avar territory to the <a href="/wiki/Gy%C5%91r" title="Győr">Győr</a>. A Lombard army under Pippin then marched into the <a href="/wiki/Drava" title="Drava">Drava</a> valley and ravaged <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>. The campaigns ended when the Saxons revolted again in 792.
</p><p>For the next two years, Charlemagne was occupied, along with the Slavs, against the Saxons. Pippin and Duke <a href="/wiki/Eric_of_Friuli" title="Eric of Friuli">Eric of Friuli</a> continued, however, to assault the Avars' ring-shaped strongholds. The great Ring of the Avars, their capital fortress, was taken twice. The booty was sent to Charlemagne at his capital, Aachen, and redistributed to his followers and to foreign rulers, including King <a href="/wiki/Offa_of_Mercia" title="Offa of Mercia">Offa of Mercia</a>. Soon the Avar <a href="/wiki/Tudun" title="Tudun">tuduns</a> had lost the will to fight and travelled to Aachen to become vassals to Charlemagne and to become Christians. Charlemagne accepted their surrender and sent one native chief, baptised Abraham, back to Avaria with the ancient title of <a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">khagan</a>. Abraham kept his people in line, but in 800, the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarians</a> under <a href="/wiki/Krum" title="Krum">Khan Krum</a> attacked the remains of the Avar state.
</p><p>In 803, Charlemagne sent a Bavarian army into <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>, defeating and bringing an end to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avar_Khaganate" title="Avar Khaganate">Avar confederation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rogers-101">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November of the same year, Charlemagne went to Regensburg where the Avar leaders acknowledged him as their ruler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rogers-101">[89]</a></sup> In 805, the Avar khagan, who had already been baptised, went to Aachen to ask permission to settle with his people south-eastward from <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rogers-101">[89]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Transdanubia" title="Transdanubia">Transdanubian</a> territories became integral parts of the Frankish realm, which was abolished by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magyars" title="Magyars">Magyars</a> in 899–900.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northeast_Slav_expeditions">Northeast Slav expeditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Northeast Slav expeditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 789, in recognition of his new pagan neighbours, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">Slavs</a>, Charlemagne marched an Austrasian-Saxon army across the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a> into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obotrite" title="Obotrite">Obotrite</a> territory. The Slavs ultimately submitted, led by their leader Witzin. Charlemagne then accepted the surrender of the <a href="/wiki/Veleti" title="Veleti">Veleti</a> under Dragovit and demanded many hostages. He also demanded permission to send missionaries into this pagan region unmolested. The army marched to the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic</a> before turning around and marching to the Rhine, winning much booty with no harassment. The tributary Slavs became loyal allies. In 795, when the Saxons broke the peace, the Abotrites and Veleti rebelled with their new ruler against the Saxons. Witzin died in battle and Charlemagne avenged him by harrying the Eastphalians on the Elbe. Thrasuco, his successor, led his men to conquest over the Nordalbingians and handed their leaders over to Charlemagne, who honoured him. The Abotrites remained loyal until Charles' death and fought later against the Danes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Slav_expeditions">Southeast Slav expeditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Southeast Slav expeditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Charlemagne incorporated much of Central Europe, he brought the Frankish state face to face with the Avars and Slavs in the southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bruce_Ross_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bruce_Ross-102">[90]</a></sup> The most southeast Frankish neighbours were <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>, who settled in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonian_Slavs#Principality" title="Pannonian Slavs">Lower Pannonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Croatia" title="Duchy of Croatia">Duchy of Croatia</a>. While fighting the Avars, the Franks had called for their support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denis_Sinor_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denis_Sinor-103">[91]</a></sup> During the 790s, he won a major victory over them in 796.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JohnVanAntwerpFinep257_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-JohnVanAntwerpFinep257-104">[92]</a></sup> Duke <a href="/wiki/Vojnomir" title="Vojnomir">Vojnomir</a> of Lower Pannonia aided Charlemagne, and the Franks made themselves overlords over the Croats of northern Dalmatia, <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a> and Pannonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JohnVanAntwerpFinep257_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-JohnVanAntwerpFinep257-104">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Frankish commander <a href="/wiki/Eric_of_Friuli" title="Eric of Friuli">Eric of Friuli</a> wanted to extend his dominion by conquering the Littoral Croat Duchy. During that time, Dalmatian Croatia was ruled by Duke <a href="/wiki/Vi%C5%A1eslav_of_Croatia" title="Višeslav of Croatia">Višeslav of Croatia</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Trsat" title="Siege of Trsat">Battle of Trsat</a>, the forces of Eric fled their positions and were routed by the forces of Višeslav.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vjekoslav_Klaić_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vjekoslav_Klaić-105">[93]</a></sup> Eric was among those killed which was a great blow for the Carolingian Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bruce_Ross_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bruce_Ross-102">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880[[Category:All_articles_with_incomplete_citations]][[Category:Articles_with_incomplete_citations_from_September_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include|&lt;span_title="A_complete_citation_is_needed.&amp;#32;(September_2020)"&gt;full_citation_needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_106-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinhard1880[[Category:All_articles_with_incomplete_citations]][[Category:Articles_with_incomplete_citations_from_September_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include|&lt;span_title="A_complete_citation_is_needed.&amp;#32;(September_2020)"&gt;full_citation_needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-106'>[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vjekoslav_Klaić_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vjekoslav_Klaić-105">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Charlemagne also directed his attention to the <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">Slavs</a> to the west of the Avar khaganate: the <a href="/wiki/Carantania" title="Carantania">Carantanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carniola" title="Carniola">Carniolans</a>. These people were subdued by the Lombards and Bavarii and made tributaries, but were never fully incorporated into the Frankish state.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperium">Imperium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Imperium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coronation">Coronation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Coronation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1901" data-file-width="2547" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg/280px-Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg/420px-Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg/560px-Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaulbach_Die_Kaiserkr%C3%B6nung_Karls_des_Gro%C3%9Fen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Imperial Coronation of Charlemagne, by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Kaulbach" title="Friedrich Kaulbach">Friedrich Kaulbach</a>, 1861</div></div></div>
<p>In 799, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_III" title="Pope Leo III">Pope Leo III</a> had been assaulted by some of the Romans, who tried to put out his eyes and tear out his tongue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[95]</a></sup> Leo escaped and fled to Charlemagne at <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shahan_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-shahan-108">[96]</a></sup> Charlemagne, advised by scholar <a href="/wiki/Alcuin" title="Alcuin">Alcuin</a>, travelled to Rome, in November 800 and held a synod. On 23 December, Leo swore an oath of innocence to Charlemagne. His position having thereby been weakened, the Pope sought to restore his status. Two days later, at <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a>, on Christmas Day (25 December), when Charlemagne knelt at the altar to pray, the Pope <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Coronation of the Holy Roman Emperor">crowned</a> him <i>Imperator Romanorum</i> ("Emperor of the Romans") in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica" title="Old Saint Peter's Basilica">Saint Peter's Basilica</a>. In so doing, the Pope rejected the legitimacy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empress_Irene" title="Empress Irene">Empress Irene</a> of Constantinople:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karel_Leo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="239" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Karel_Leo.jpg/170px-Karel_Leo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/56/Karel_Leo.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karel_Leo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_III" title="Pope Leo III">Pope Leo III</a>, crowning Charlemagne from <i>Chroniques de France ou de Saint Denis</i>, vol. 1; France, second quarter of 14th century.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>When <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">Odoacer</a> compelled the abdication of <a href="/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus" title="Romulus Augustulus">Romulus Augustulus</a>, he did not abolish the Western Empire as a separate power, but caused it to be reunited with or sink into the Eastern, so that from that time there was a single undivided Roman Empire ... [Pope Leo III and Charlemagne], like their predecessors, held the Roman Empire to be one and indivisible, and proposed by the coronation of [Charlemagne] not to proclaim a severance of the East and West ... they were not revolting against a reigning sovereign, but legitimately filling up the place of the deposed <a href="/wiki/Constantine_VI" title="Constantine VI">Constantine VI</a> ... [Charlemagne] was held to be the legitimate successor, not of Romulus Augustulus, but of Constantine VI ...<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[97]</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>Charlemagne's coronation as Emperor, though intended to represent the continuation of the unbroken line of Emperors from <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> to Constantine VI, had the effect of setting up two separate (and often opposing) Empires and two separate claims to imperial authority. It led to war in 802, and for centuries to come, <a href="/wiki/Problem_of_two_emperors" title="Problem of two emperors">the Emperors of both West and East would make competing claims of sovereignty over the whole.</a>
</p><p>Einhard says that Charlemagne was ignorant of the Pope's intent and did not want any such coronation:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>[H]e at first had such an aversion that he declared that he would not have set foot in the Church the day that they [the imperial titles] were conferred, although it was a great feast-day, if he could have foreseen the design of the Pope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[98]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>A number of modern scholars, however,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[99]</a></sup> suggest that Charlemagne was indeed aware of the coronation; certainly, he cannot have missed the bejewelled crown waiting on the altar when he came to pray—something even contemporary sources support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Debate">Debate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Debate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5781" data-file-width="3479" decoding="async" height="399" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg/240px-Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg/360px-Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg/480px-Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aachener_Dom_BW_2016-07-09_13-49-15.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Throne_of_Charlemagne" title="Throne of Charlemagne">Throne of Charlemagne</a> and the subsequent German Kings in <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral" title="Aachen Cathedral">Aachen Cathedral</a>, Germany</div></div></div>
<p>Historians have debated for centuries whether Charlemagne was aware before the coronation of the Pope's intention to crown him Emperor (Charlemagne declared that he would not have entered Saint Peter's had he known, according to chapter twenty-eight of Einhard's <i>Vita Karoli Magni</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[101]</a></sup> but that debate obscured the more significant question of <i>why</i> the Pope granted the title and why Charlemagne accepted it.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Roger_Collins" title="Roger Collins">Collins</a> points out "[t]hat the motivation behind the acceptance of the imperial title was a romantic and antiquarian interest in reviving the Roman Empire is highly unlikely."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987147_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987147-114">[102]</a></sup> For one thing, such romance would not have appealed either to Franks or Roman Catholics at the turn of the ninth century, both of whom viewed the <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">Classical</a> heritage of the Roman Empire with distrust. The Franks took pride in having "fought against and thrown from their shoulders the heavy yoke of the Romans" and "from the knowledge gained in baptism, clothed in gold and precious stones the bodies of the holy martyrs whom the Romans had killed by fire, by the sword and by wild animals", as <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Short" title="Pepin the Short">Pepin III</a> described it in a law of 763 or 764.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987151_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987151-115">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Furthermore, the new title—carrying with it the risk that the new emperor would "make drastic changes to the traditional styles and procedures of government" or "concentrate his attentions on Italy or on Mediterranean concerns more generally"—risked alienating the Frankish leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987149_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987149-116">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>For both the Pope and Charlemagne, the Roman Empire remained a significant power in European politics at this time. The <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, based in Constantinople, continued to hold a substantial portion of Italy, with borders not far south of Rome. Charles' sitting in judgment of the Pope could be seen as usurping the prerogatives of the Emperor in Constantinople:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>By whom, however, could he [the Pope] be tried? Who, in other words, was qualified to pass judgement on the Vicar of Christ? In normal circumstances the only conceivable answer to that question would have been the Emperor at Constantinople; but the imperial throne was at this moment occupied by <a href="/wiki/Irene_of_Athens" title="Irene of Athens">Irene</a>. That the Empress was notorious for having blinded and murdered her own son was, in the minds of both Leo and Charles, almost immaterial: it was enough that she was a woman. The female sex was known to be incapable of governing, and by the old Salic tradition was debarred from doing so. As far as Western Europe was concerned, the Throne of the Emperors was vacant: Irene's claim to it was merely an additional proof, if any were needed, of the degradation into which the so-called Roman Empire had fallen.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/John_Julius_Norwich" title="John Julius Norwich">John Julius Norwich</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorwich1992b378_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorwich1992b378-117">[105]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_(German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2769" data-file-width="4923" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_%28German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/290px-Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_%28German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_%28German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/435px-Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_%28German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_%28German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/580px-Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_%28German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Julius_Schnorr_von_Carolsfeld_(German_-_The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coronation of Charlemagne, drawing by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julius_Schnorr_von_Karolsfeld" title="Julius Schnorr von Karolsfeld">Julius Schnorr von Karolsfeld</a></div></div></div>
<p>For the Pope, then, there was "no living Emperor at that time"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorwich1992b379_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorwich1992b379-118">[106]</a></sup> though <a href="/wiki/Henri_Pirenne" title="Henri Pirenne">Henri Pirenne</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPirenne2012234n_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPirenne2012234n-119">[107]</a></sup> disputes this saying that the coronation "was not in any sense explained by the fact that at this moment a woman was reigning in Constantinople". Nonetheless, the Pope took the extraordinary step of creating one. The papacy had since 727 been in conflict with Irene's predecessors in Constantinople over a number of issues, chiefly the continued Byzantine adherence to the doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Iconoclasm" title="Iconoclasm">iconoclasm</a>, the destruction of Christian images; while from 750, the secular power of the Byzantine Empire in central Italy had been nullified.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1209" data-file-width="934" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg/240px-Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg/360px-Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg/480px-Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Couronnement_d%27un_prince_-_Sacramentaire_de_Charles_le_Chauve_Lat1141_f2v.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coronation of an idealised king, depicted in the Sacramentary of <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bald" title="Charles the Bald">Charles the Bald</a> (about 870)</div></div></div>
<p>By bestowing the Imperial crown upon Charlemagne, the Pope arrogated to himself "the right to appoint ... the Emperor of the Romans, ... establishing the imperial crown as his own personal gift but simultaneously granting himself implicit superiority over the Emperor whom he had created." And "because the Byzantines had proved so unsatisfactory from every point of view—political, military and doctrinal—he would select a westerner: the one man who by his wisdom and statesmanship and the vastness of his dominions ... stood out head and shoulders above his contemporaries."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>With Charlemagne's coronation, therefore, "the Roman Empire remained, so far as either of them [Charlemagne and Leo] were concerned, one and indivisible, with Charles as its Emperor", though there can have been "little doubt that the coronation, with all that it implied, would be furiously contested in Constantinople".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorwich1992a3_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorwich1992a3-121">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alcuin" title="Alcuin">Alcuin</a> writes hopefully in his letters of an <i>Imperium Christianum</i> ("Christian Empire"), wherein, "just as the inhabitants of the [Roman Empire] had been united by a common Roman citizenship", presumably this new empire would be united by a common Christian faith.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987151_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987151-115">[103]</a></sup> This is the view of Pirenne when he says "Charles was the Emperor of the <i>ecclesia</i> as the Pope conceived it, of the Roman Church, regarded as the universal Church".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPirenne2012233_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPirenne2012233-122">[110]</a></sup> The <i>Imperium Christianum</i> was further supported at a number of <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">synods</a> all across Europe by Paulinus of Aquileia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Butler1995_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Butler1995-123">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>What is known, from the Byzantine chronicler <a href="/wiki/Theophanes_the_Confessor" title="Theophanes the Confessor">Theophanes</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1987153_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1987153-124">[112]</a></sup> is that Charlemagne's reaction to his coronation was to take the initial steps towards securing the Constantinopolitan throne by sending envoys of marriage to Irene, and that Irene reacted somewhat favourably to them.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="775" data-file-width="920" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg/290px-Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg/435px-Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg/580px-Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raphael_Charlemagne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Coronation_of_Charlemagne" title="The Coronation of Charlemagne">The Coronation of Charlemagne</a></i>, by assistants of <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">Raphael</a>, c. 1516–1517</div></div></div>
<p>It is important to distinguish between the universalist and localist conceptions of the empire, which remain controversial among historians. According to the former, the empire was a universal monarchy, a "commonwealth of the whole world, whose sublime unity transcended every minor distinction"; and the emperor "was entitled to the obedience of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>". According to the latter, the emperor had no ambition for universal dominion; his realm was limited in the same way as that of every other ruler, and when he made more far-reaching claims his object was normally to ward off the attacks either of the Pope or of the Byzantine emperor. According to this view, also, the origin of the empire is to be explained by specific local circumstances rather than by overarching theories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Ohnsorge, for a long time, it had been the custom of Byzantium to designate the German princes as spiritual "sons" of the Romans. What might have been acceptable in the fifth century had become provoking and insulting to the Franks in the eighth century. Charles came to believe that the Roman emperor, who claimed to head the world hierarchy of states, was, in reality, no greater than Charles himself, a king as other kings, since beginning in 629 he had entitled himself "Basileus" (translated literally as "king"). Ohnsorge finds it significant that the chief wax seal of Charles, which bore only the inscription: "Christe, protege Carolum regem Francorum [Christ, protect Charles, king of the Franks], was used from 772 to 813, even during the imperial period and was not replaced by a special imperial seal; indicating that Charles felt himself to be just the king of the Franks. Finally, Ohnsorge points out that in the spring of 813 at Aachen Charles crowned his only surviving son, Louis, as the emperor without recourse to Rome with only the acclamation of his Franks. The form in which this acclamation was offered was Frankish-Christian rather than Roman. This implies both independence from Rome and a Frankish (non-Roman) understanding of empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>May-Harting argues that the Imperial title was Charlemagne's face-saving offer to incorporate the recently conquered Saxons. Since the Saxons did not have an institution of kingship for their own ethnicity, claiming the right to rule them as King of the Saxons was not possible. Hence, it is argued, Charlemagne used the supra-ethnic Imperial title to incorporate the Saxons, which helped to cement the diverse peoples under his rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_title">Imperial title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Imperial title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Charlemagne used these circumstances to claim that he was the <a href="/wiki/Renovatio_imperii_Romanorum" title="Renovatio imperii Romanorum">"renewer of the Roman Empire"</a>, which had declined under the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>. In his official charters, Charles preferred the style <i>Karolus serenissimus Augustus a Deo coronatus magnus pacificus imperator Romanum gubernans imperium</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[116]</a></sup> ("Charles, most serene Augustus crowned by God, the great, peaceful emperor ruling the Roman empire") to the more direct <i>Imperator Romanorum</i> ("Emperor of the Romans").
</p><p>The title of Emperor remained in the Carolingian family for years to come, but divisions of territory and in-fighting over supremacy of the Frankish state weakened its significance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECantor2015194–95,_212_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECantor2015194–95,_212-129">[117]</a></sup> The papacy itself never forgot the title nor abandoned the right to bestow it. When the family of Charles ceased to produce worthy heirs, the Pope gladly crowned whichever Italian magnate could best protect him from his local enemies. The empire would remain in continuous existence for over a millennium, as the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, a true imperial successor to Charles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1996316–17_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1996316–17-130">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_diplomacy">Imperial diplomacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Imperial diplomacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_814.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="919" data-file-width="1399" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Europe_814.svg/260px-Europe_814.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Europe_814.svg/390px-Europe_814.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Europe_814.svg/520px-Europe_814.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_814.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Europe at the death of the Charlemagne 814.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iconoclasm_(Byzantine)" title="Iconoclasm (Byzantine)">iconoclasm of the Byzantine</a> <a href="/wiki/Leo_III_the_Isaurian" title="Leo III the Isaurian">Isaurian Dynasty</a> was endorsed by the Franks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Becher2011_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Becher2011-131">[119]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_Council_of_Nicaea" title="Second Council of Nicaea">Second Council of Nicaea</a> reintroduced the veneration of icons under Empress <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empress_Irene" title="Byzantine Empress Irene">Irene</a>. The council was not recognised by Charlemagne since no Frankish emissaries had been invited, even though Charlemagne ruled more than three provinces of the classical Roman empire and was considered equal in rank to the Byzantine emperor. And while the Pope supported the reintroduction of the iconic veneration, he politically digressed from Byzantium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Becher2011_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-Becher2011-131">[119]</a></sup> He certainly desired to increase the influence of the papacy, to honour his saviour Charlemagne, and to solve the constitutional issues then most troubling to European jurists in an era when Rome was not in the hands of an emperor. Thus, Charlemagne's assumption of the imperial title was not a usurpation in the eyes of the Franks or Italians. It was, however, seen as such in Byzantium, where it was protested by Irene and her successor <a href="/wiki/Nikephoros_I" title="Nikephoros I">Nikephoros I</a>—neither of whom had any great effect in enforcing their protests.
</p><p>The East Romans, however, still held several territories in Italy: Venice (what was left of the <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_Ravenna" title="Exarchate of Ravenna">Exarchate of Ravenna</a>), <a href="/wiki/Reggio_Calabria" title="Reggio Calabria">Reggio</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabria</a>), <a href="/wiki/Otranto" title="Otranto">Otranto</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">Apulia</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a> (the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ducatus_Neapolitanus" title="Ducatus Neapolitanus">Ducatus Neapolitanus</a></i>). These regions remained outside of Frankish hands until 804, when the Venetians, torn by infighting, transferred their allegiance to the Iron Crown of Pippin, Charles' son. The <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Nicephori" title="Pax Nicephori">Pax Nicephori</a></i> ended. Nicephorus ravaged the coasts with a fleet, initiating the only instance of war between the Byzantines and the Franks. The conflict lasted until 810 when the pro-Byzantine party in Venice gave their city back to the Byzantine Emperor, and the two emperors of Europe made peace: Charlemagne received the <a href="/wiki/Istria" title="Istria">Istrian</a> peninsula and in 812 the emperor <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_Rangabe" title="Michael I Rangabe">Michael I Rangabe</a> recognised his status as Emperor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[120]</a></sup> although not necessarily as "Emperor of the Romans".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eichmann1942_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eichmann1942-133">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Danish_attacks">Danish attacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Danish attacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the conquest of Nordalbingia, the Frankish frontier was brought into contact with Scandinavia. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_paganism" title="Norse paganism">pagan</a> Danes, "a race almost unknown to his ancestors, but destined to be only too well known to his sons" as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Oman" title="Charles Oman">Charles Oman</a> described them, inhabiting the <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a> peninsula, had heard many stories from Widukind and his allies who had taken refuge with them about the dangers of the Franks and the fury which their Christian king could direct against pagan neighbours.
</p><p>In 808, the king of the Danes, <a href="/wiki/Gudfred" title="Gudfred">Godfred</a>, expanded the vast <a href="/wiki/Danevirke" title="Danevirke">Danevirke</a> across the isthmus of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schleswig" title="Schleswig">Schleswig</a>. This defence, last employed in the Danish-Prussian War of 1864, was at its beginning a 30 km (19 mi) long earthenwork rampart. The Danevirke protected Danish land and gave Godfred the opportunity to harass <a href="/wiki/Frisia" title="Frisia">Frisia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a> with pirate raids. He also subdued the Frank-allied Veleti and fought the Abotrites.
</p><p>Godfred invaded Frisia, joked of visiting Aachen, but was murdered before he could do any more, either by a Frankish assassin or by one of his own men. Godfred was succeeded by his nephew <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Hemming" title="King Hemming">Hemming</a>, who concluded the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Heiligen" title="Treaty of Heiligen">Treaty of Heiligen</a> with Charlemagne in late 811.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Testament_of_Charlemagne" title="Testament of Charlemagne">Testament of Charlemagne</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:632px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AachenerDomSarg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="929" data-file-width="2883" decoding="async" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/AachenerDomSarg.jpg/630px-AachenerDomSarg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/AachenerDomSarg.jpg/945px-AachenerDomSarg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/AachenerDomSarg.jpg/1260px-AachenerDomSarg.jpg 2x" width="630"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AachenerDomSarg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Proserpina_sarcophagus" title="Proserpina sarcophagus">Proserpina sarcophagus</a> of Charlemagne in the <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral_Treasury" title="Aachen Cathedral Treasury">Aachen Cathedral Treasury</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2057" data-file-width="2019" decoding="async" height="265" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg/260px-Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg/390px-Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg/520px-Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shroud_of_Charlemagne_manufactured_in_Constantinople_814.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A portion of the 814 death <a href="/wiki/Shroud" title="Shroud">shroud</a> of Charlemagne. It represents a <a href="/wiki/Quadriga" title="Quadriga">quadriga</a> and was manufactured in <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_Cluny" title="Musée de Cluny">Musée de Cluny</a>, Paris.</div></div></div>
<p>In 813, Charlemagne called <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a>, king of <a href="/wiki/Aquitaine" title="Aquitaine">Aquitaine</a>, his only surviving legitimate son, to his court. There Charlemagne crowned his son as co-emperor and sent him back to Aquitaine. He then spent the autumn hunting before returning to Aachen on 1 November. In January, he fell ill with <a href="/wiki/Pleurisy" title="Pleurisy">pleurisy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[122]</a></sup> In deep depression (mostly because many of his plans were not yet realised), he took to his bed on 21 January and as <a href="/wiki/Einhard" title="Einhard">Einhard</a> tells it:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>He died January twenty-eighth, the seventh day from the time that he took to his bed, at nine o'clock in the morning, after partaking of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Communion" title="Holy Communion">Holy Communion</a>, in the seventy-second year of his age and the forty-seventh of his reign.</p></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3120" data-file-width="4160" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg/260px-Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg/390px-Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg/520px-Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karlsschrein_front_side_left.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II's</a> gold and silver casket for Charlemagne, the <a href="/wiki/Karlsschrein" title="Karlsschrein">Karlsschrein</a></div></div></div>
<p>He was buried that same day, in <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral" title="Aachen Cathedral">Aachen Cathedral</a>. The earliest surviving <i><a href="/wiki/Planctus" title="Planctus">planctus</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Planctus_de_obitu_Karoli" title="Planctus de obitu Karoli">Planctus de obitu Karoli</a></i>, was composed by a monk of <a href="/wiki/Bobbio_Abbey" title="Bobbio Abbey">Bobbio</a>, which he had patronised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Godman1985_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Godman1985-135">[123]</a></sup> A later story, told by Otho of Lomello, Count of the Palace at Aachen in the time of <a href="/wiki/Otto_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto III, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Otto III</a>, would claim that he and Otto had discovered Charlemagne's tomb: Charlemagne, they claimed, was seated upon a throne, wearing a crown and holding a sceptre, his flesh almost entirely incorrupt. In 1165, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Frederick_I" title="Emperor Frederick I">Emperor Frederick I</a> re-opened the tomb again and placed the emperor in a sarcophagus beneath the floor of the cathedral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[124]</a></sup> In 1215 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Frederick_II" title="Emperor Frederick II">Emperor Frederick II</a> re-interred him in a casket made of gold and silver known as the <a href="/wiki/Karlsschrein" title="Karlsschrein">Karlsschrein</a>.
</p><p>Charlemagne's death emotionally affected many of his subjects, particularly those of the literary clique who had surrounded him at Aachen. An anonymous monk of Bobbio lamented:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDutton2004_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDutton2004-137">[125]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>From the lands where the sun rises to western shores, people are crying and wailing ... the Franks, the Romans, all Christians, are stung with mourning and great worry ... the young and old, glorious nobles, all lament the loss of their Caesar ... the world laments the death of Charles ... O Christ, you who govern the heavenly host, grant a peaceful place to Charles in your kingdom. Alas for miserable me.</p></blockquote>
<p>Louis succeeded him as Charles had intended. He left <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Testament_of_Charlemagne" title="The Testament of Charlemagne">a testament</a> allocating his assets in 811 that was not updated prior to his death. He left most of his wealth to the Church, to be used for charity. His empire lasted only another generation in its entirety; its division, according to custom, between Louis's own sons after their father's death laid the foundation for the modern states of Germany and France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire#Government" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire § Government</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Carolingian king exercised the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bannum" title="Bannum">bannum</a></i>, the right to rule and command. Under the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, it was a royal prerogative but could be delegated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evergates1983_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evergates1983-139">[127]</a></sup> He had supreme jurisdiction in judicial matters, made legislation, led the army, and protected both the Church and the poor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> His administration was an attempt to organise the kingdom, church and nobility around him. As an administrator, Charlemagne stands out for his many reforms: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monetary" title="Monetary">monetary</a>, governmental, military, cultural and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecclesiastic" title="Ecclesiastic">ecclesiastical</a>. He is the main protagonist of the "Carolingian Renaissance".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Charlemagne's success rested primarily on novel <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">siege</a> technologies and excellent logistics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowlus2006_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bowlus2006-140">[128]</a></sup> rather than the long-claimed "<a href="/wiki/Heavy_cavalry" title="Heavy cavalry">cavalry</a> revolution" led by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Martel" title="Charles Martel">Charles Martel</a> in 730s. However, the <a href="/wiki/Stirrup" title="Stirrup">stirrup</a>, which made the "shock cavalry" <a href="/wiki/Lance" title="Lance">lance</a> charge possible, was not introduced to the Frankish kingdom until the late eighth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-141">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Horses were used extensively by the Frankish military because they provided a quick, long-distance method of <a href="/wiki/Mounted_infantry" title="Mounted infantry">transporting troops</a>, which was critical to building and maintaining the large empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-141">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_and_monetary_reforms">Economic and monetary reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlemagne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Economic and monetary reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karldergrossesignatur.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="624" decoding="async" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Karldergrossesignatur.svg/330px-Karldergrossesignatur.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Karldergrossesignatur.svg/495px-Karldergrossesignatur.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Karldergrossesignatur.svg/660px-Karldergrossesignatur.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karldergrossesignatur.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Monogram" title="Monogram">Monogram</a> of Charlemagne, including <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Signum_manus" title="Signum manus">signum manus</a></i></span>, from the subscription of a royal diploma: <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Signum</i></span> (monogr.: KAROLVS) <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Karoli gloriosissimi regis</i></span></div></div></div>
<p>Charlemagne had an important role in determining Europe's immediate economic future. Pursuing his father's reforms, Charlemagne abolished the monetary system based on the gold <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/Solidus_(coin)" title="Solidus (coin)">sou</a></i></span>. Instead, he and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_monarchs" title="Anglo-Saxon monarchs">Anglo-Saxon King</a> <a href="/wiki/Offa_of_Mercia" title="Offa of Mercia">Offa of Mercia</a> took up Pippin's system for pragmatic reasons, notably a shortage of the metal.
</p><p>The gold shortage was a direct consequence of the conclusion of peace with Byzantium, which resulted in ceding Venice and Sicily to the East and losing their trade routes to Africa. The resulting standardisation economically harmonised and unified the complex array of currencies that had been in use at the commencement of his reign, thus simplifying trade and commerce.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="666" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg/170px-Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg/255px-Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg/340px-Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_denier_Tours_793_to_812.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Denier from the era of Charlemagne, <a href="/wiki/Tours" title="Tours">Tours</a>, 793–812</div></div></div>
<p>Charlemagne established a new standard, the <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/French_livre" title="French livre">livre carolinienne</a></i></span> (from the Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_units_of_measurement" title="Ancient Roman units of measurement">libra</a></i></span>, the modern <a href="/wiki/Pound_(currency)" title="Pound (currency)">pound</a>), which was based upon a pound of silver—a unit of both money and weight—worth 20 sous (from the Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Solidus_(coin)" title="Solidus (coin)">solidus</a></i></span> [which was primarily an accounting device and never actually minted], the modern <a href="/wiki/Shilling" title="Shilling">shilling</a>) or 240 <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denier_(coin)" title="Denier (coin)">deniers</a></i></span> (from the Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Denarius" title="Denarius">denarius</a></i></span>, the modern <a href="/wiki/Penny" title="Penny">penny</a>). During this period, the <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">livre</i></span> and the <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">sou</i></span> were counting units; only the <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">denier</i></span> was a coin of the realm.
